    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 10.4 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          7.38 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.12 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 59.9 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 77.8% of the total average of 77.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 34.2 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          2.06 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.03 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 55.3 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 78.5% of the total average of 70.4 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 32.4 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.42 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.03 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 24.3 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 52.7% of the total average of 46.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 12.8 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 12.6 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 33.9 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.38 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.03 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 22.4 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 47.8% of the total average of 46.9 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 15.8 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 33.6% of the total average of 46.9   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 11.7 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 11.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

          issues an instruction every 48.7 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.42 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.02 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 34.9 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 50.6% of the total average of 68.9 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 24.9 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 36.2% of the total average of 68.9   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 17.5 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 17.2 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 24.1 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          2.04 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.05 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 31.8 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 64.9% of the total average of 49.0 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.                                                                                  
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 22.7 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 21.2 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 27.8 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          2.00 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        19,26
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 39.1 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 70.4% of the total average of 55.6 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.                                                                                  
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 20.6 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 19.3 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 29.7 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.96 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    20,03
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        18,71
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 41.7 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 71.6% of the total average of 58.2 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.                                                                                  
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 20.0 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 18.7 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 33.5 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.93 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.03 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------

    Section: Scheduler Statistics
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Instructions Per Active Issue Slot                                          inst/cycle                              1
    One or More Eligible                                                                 %                           3,85
    Issued Warp Per Scheduler                                                                                        0,04
    No Eligible                                                                          %                          96,15
    Theoretical Warps Per Scheduler                                                   warp                              8
    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,27
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,04
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 26.0 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.27 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.    

    Section: Warp State Statistics
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Warp Cycles Per Issued Instruction                                               cycle                          33,07

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 11.6 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 35.2% of the total average of 33.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 13.7 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 41.5% of the total average of 33.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 6.7 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          6.6 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    Section: Scheduler Statistics
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Instructions Per Active Issue Slot                                          inst/cycle                              1
    One or More Eligible                                                                 %                           2,74
    Issued Warp Per Scheduler                                                                                        0,03
    No Eligible                                                                          %                          97,26
    Theoretical Warps Per Scheduler                                                   warp                              8
    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,57
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,03
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 36.6 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.57 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.03 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 35.3 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 61.6% of the total average of 57.3 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 16.6 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 16.4 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Instructions Per Active Issue Slot                                          inst/cycle                              1
    One or More Eligible                                                                 %                           2,13
    Issued Warp Per Scheduler                                                                                        0,02
    No Eligible                                                                          %                          97,87
    Theoretical Warps Per Scheduler                                                   warp                              8
    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,72
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,02
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 47.0 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.72 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.02 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 58.4 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 72.4% of the total average of 80.6 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Instructions Per Active Issue Slot                                          inst/cycle                              1
    One or More Eligible                                                                 %                           6,40
    Issued Warp Per Scheduler                                                                                        0,06
    No Eligible                                                                          %                          93,60
    Theoretical Warps Per Scheduler                                                   warp                              8
    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,99
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,07
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 15.6 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.99 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.07 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    27,35
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        25,56
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 14.1 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 45.3% of the total average of 31.1 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.
